<div

<h2>Editorial
Reviews</h2>





<div
class="content">






<h3
class="productDescriptionSource">Amazon.com</h3>






<div
class="productDescriptionWrapper">







Better
known
as
the
&quot;White
Album,&quot;
this
was
meant
to
be
the
record
that
brought
them
back
to
earth
after
three
years
of
studio
experimentation.
Instead,
it
took
them
all
over
the
place,
continuing
to
burst
the
envelope
of
pop
music.
Lennon
and
McCartney
were
still
at
the
height
of
their
powers,
with
Lennon
in
particular
growing
into
one
of
rock's
towering
figures.
But
even
McCartney
could
still
rock,
and
the
amazement
on
&quot;Helter
Skelter&quot;
was
that
he
had
vocal
cords
at
the
end.
From
Beach
Boys
knock-offs
to
reggae
and
to
the
unknown
(&quot;Revolution
#9&quot;),
this
has
it
all.
Some
records
have







<i>legend</i>
written
all
over
them;
this
is
one.







<i>--Chris
Nickson</i>







<div
class="emptyClear">







</div>






</div>






<h3
class="productDescriptionSource">Product
Description</h3>






<div
class="productDescriptionWrapper">







The
classic
original
Beatles
studio
albums
have
been
re-mastered
by
a
dedicated
team
of
engineers
at
Abbey
Road
Studios
in
London
over
a
four
year
period
utilising
state
of
the
art
recording
technology
alongside
vintage
studio
equipment,
carefully
maintaining
the
authenticity
and
integrity
of
the
original
analogue
recordings.
The
result
of
this
painstaking
process
is
the
highest
fidelity
the
Beatles
catalogue
has
seen
since
its
original
release.






<p><br
/>
<br
/>Within
each
CD's
new
packaging,
booklets
include
detailed
historical
notes
along
with
informative
recording
notes.
For
a
limited
period,
each
CD
will
also
be
embedded
with
a
brief
documentary
film
about
the
album.
The
newly
produced
mini-documentaries
on
the
making
of
each
album,
directed
by
Bob
Smeaton,
are
included
as
QuickTime
files
on
each
album.
The
documentaries
contain
archival
footage,
rare
photographs
and
never-before-heard
studio
chat
from
The
Beatles,
offering
a
unique
and
very
personal
insight
into
the
studio
atmosphere.
</p>

class="emptyClear">







</div>

</div>

=

Reviews</strong>

<div
id="revMHRL"
class="mb30">










<div
id="rev-dpReviewsMostHelpful-R170AARLNZ9D3M"
class="reviews">











<div
class="gry

of

review

</div>











<div
class="clearboth"></div>











<div
class="mt4
ttl">











<span
class="swSprite
s_star_5_0
"
title="5.0
out
of
5
stars"><span>5.0
out
of
5
stars</span></span>












<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R170AARLNZ9D3M/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/187-8143282-8173756?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B0025KVLU6&amp;nodeID=5174&amp;store=music"
class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>You'll
never
crack
the
code</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">May
14,
2003</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/pdp/profile/AGH5RJDNL7TAZ/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/187-8143282-8173756"
class="noTextDecoration">John
Stodder</a></span>
</span>











</div>











<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













There
are
a
few
albums
from
the
rock
era
that
I
feel
I've
been
in
a
relationship
with
since
the
first
day
I
got
them.
&quot;The
Beatles&quot;
is
one
of
those
albums.
I
found
it
under
my
Christmas
tree
in
1968,
and
I've
been
engaged
with
it
at
some
level
ever
since.
It
is
not
the
best
Beatles
album,
objectively;
nor
is
it
my
favorite.
But
it
has
always
compelled
my
attention.













<p>At
the
time
it
came
out,
I
was
12,
but
even
then
it
was
clear
that
we
were
no
longer
in
Pepperland
or
on
a
Magical
Mystery
Tour.
This
album
wasn't
yet
more
&quot;progress&quot;
toward
some
new
musical
form.
Musically,
it
embraced
values
never
before
associated
with
the
Beatles
as
I
understood
them:
Parody,
pastiche,
rock
and
roll
revivalism,
music-hall
nostalgia,
avant-garde
experimentation,
political
agitation,
intimate
confession,
trivial
nonsense.
It
is,
simply,
a
series
of
highly
personal
statements
from
the
three
songwriters,
coalescing
around
no
particular
theme
other
than
the
right
to
personal
expression.
</p>












<p>&quot;The
Beatles&quot;
is
not,
to
me,
&quot;the
sound
of
the
Beatles
breaking
up.&quot;
That's
the
storyline
a
lot
of
Beatle
historians
apply
to
this
album.
If
they're
basing
this
judgement
on
the
fact
that
the
individual
songwriters'
imprints
are
on
each
song,
you'd
have
to
argue
that
the
breakup
began
much
earlier,
around
the
time
of
&quot;Beatles
for
Sale&quot;
or
&quot;Help!&quot;
Lennon-McCartney
were
rarely
a
songwriting
&quot;team&quot;
in
the
sense
of
George
and
Ira
Gershwin.
Their
partnership
was
always
about
strategy,
i.e.
how
to
ensure
that
third-rate
songs
would
not
be
included
on
albums
just
for
the
sake
of
fairness.
&quot;The
Beatles&quot;
instead
simply
shows
the
evolution
of
each
of
the
three
songwriters
(on
this
album,
George
emerges
dramatically)
as
they
each
embraced
new
musical
ideas
and
applied
their
life
experiences
to
their
art.
Having
helped
break
all
the
molds
for
what
was
acceptable
songwriting
in
their
previous
work,
they
each
now
proceeded
to
take
full
advantage
of
the
freedom
they'd
won.
Some
of
the
dumber
cuts
on
&quot;The
Beatles&quot;
demonstrate,
perhaps,
the
expression
&quot;freedom's
just
another
word
for
nothing
left
to
lose.&quot;
Paul,
in
particular,
seemed
frightened
to
step
out
too
often
without
the
crutch
of
some
existing
form
that
he
could
parody
or
pay
tribute
to,
i.e.
&quot;Honey
Pie,&quot;
&quot;Back
in
the
USSR&quot;
or
&quot;Rocky
Racoon.&quot;
But,
while
you
can
say
that,
you
have
to
acknowledge
that
in
this
massive
album,
there
are
perhaps
half
a
dozen
Paul
songs
that
are
among
his
best
and
most
original:
&quot;I
Will,&quot;
&quot;Blackbird,&quot;
&quot;Mother
Nature's
Son,&quot;
&quot;Helter
Skelter&quot;
for
four
examples.
</p>












<p>Lennon's
direction
was
to
become
more
nakedly
confessional,
as
befits
someone
who
was
dealing
with
such
turbulent
emotions
at
the
time.
He
gives
us
some
of
his
most
beautiful
songs,
like
&quot;Dear
Prudence,&quot;
and
some
of
his
most
intense,
like
&quot;I'm
So
Tired,&quot;
&quot;Revolution,&quot;
&quot;Yer
Blues,&quot;
and
&quot;Sexy
Sadie.&quot;
Often,
as
in
&quot;The
Continuing
Story
of
Bungalow
Bill,&quot;
&quot;Glass
Onion,&quot;
or
&quot;Everybody
Has
Something
to
Hide
Except
for
Me
and
My
Monkey,&quot;
he
seems
to
be
writing
in
code,
and
that
sense
of
allusiveness
gives
the
album
much
of
its
cracked
character.
And
of
course,
he's
the
guy
who
assembled
the
collage,
&quot;Revolution
9,&quot;
which
is
to
rock
and
roll
what
&quot;Finnegans
Wake&quot;
is
to
English
literature--a
dream
that
floats
between
meaning
and
nothingness.
</p>












<p>George
seems
to
be
captured
here
in
a
moment
of
great
self-discovery
as
an
artist;
you
can
hear
his
talent
finally
come
together
in
&quot;While
My
Guitar
Gently
Weeps,&quot;
which
I
remember
at
age
12
was
to
my
ears
the
best
thing
on
the
album--and
still
seems
to
be
so.
Prior
to
the
White
Album,
he
had
these
cautious
little
songs
on
the
early
albums,
and
then
embraced
India,
which
while
sometimes
satisfying
seemed
weird
and
out
of
place.
His
songs
here
sets
the
stage
for
&quot;Something,&quot;
&quot;Here
Comes
the
Sun&quot;
and
then
his
monumental
early
solo
work.
At
age
12,
I
thought
&quot;Long,
Long,
Long&quot;
was
a
emotional
powerhouse--and
I
still
do.</p>












<p>A
few
months
after
I
got
&quot;The
Beatles,&quot;
the
Charles
Manson
murders
took
place,
and
eventually
the
DA
made
the
case
that
somehow,
insanely,
the
murders
were
inspired
by
songs
on
this
album.
Around
the
same
time,
the
media
were
full
of
bizarre
speculation
that
Paul
McCartney
was
dead,
and
that
clues
were
all
over
this
album.
It's
no
accident
that
half-insane
people
might
mine
&quot;The
Beatles&quot;
for
hidden
messages
and
evidence
of
conspiracies.
The
world
it
depicts
is
strange
and
almost
claustrophobic--all
the
more
so
for
its
haphazard
approach
and
its
odd
switches
in
tone
from
childish
delight
to
fiendish
paranoia.
But
even
those
of
us
who
live
normal
lives
and
dream
normal
dreams
can
acknowledge
that
&quot;The
Beatles&quot;
has
a
hold
on
your
consciousness
that
is
unlike
anything
else
the
group
did,
and
unlike
anything
else
that
came
out
of
the
rock
era.
</p>











</div>











</div>

</div>











<div
class="clearboth"></div>











<div
class="mt4
ttl">











<span
class="swSprite
s_star_5_0
"
title="5.0
out
of
5
stars"><span>5.0
out
of
5
stars</span></span>












<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/review/R32QQRFHJ5A7WL/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/187-8143282-8173756?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B0025KVLU6&amp;nodeID=5174&amp;store=music"
class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>NOT
REMASTERED</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">March
15,
2000</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/pdp/profile/AICRDGOQ9KCVA/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/187-8143282-8173756"
class="noTextDecoration">&quot;gordon@ruraltel.net&quot;</a></span>
</span>











</div>











<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













To
all
the
golden
eared
audiophiles
who
can
hear
all
the
differences
in
this
30th
Anniversery
reissue,
I
say,
what
a
bunch
of
whooee.
This
is
the
EXACT
SAME
MASTER
as
the
1987
release.
No
difference...NADA.
Please
notice,
the
Amazon
listing
has
been
changed
from
&quot;remastered&quot;
to
&quot;original
recording.&quot;
It's
amazing
how
much
psycology
is
at
work
when
people
listen.
If
they
believe
it's
remastered,
their
ear
will
trick
them
into
believing
it
sounds
different.
Don't
believe
it.












<p>So,
that
means
all
of
us
Beatle
fans
have
forked
over
thiry-some
odd
dollars
for
the
exact
same
product
that
we
had.
The
question
is,
Capital/EMI,
why
the
H
didn't
you
remaster
this?
The
white
album
is
one
of
the
most
poorly
remastered
discs
in
the
Beatles
catalog
(but
it's
got
some
stiff
competition,
the
first
four
albums
for
starters).
It's
unfathomable
to
me
that
Capital/EMI
would
ask
Beatles
fans
to
shell
out
that
kind
of
money
for
an
unimproved
product,
and
a
product
that
sorely
needed
improvement.
What,
we're
supposed
to
be
happy
to
pay
over
thirty
dollars
for
ridiculous
miniture
artwork
which
you
need
a
magnifying
glass
to
read
and
see?
Come
on,
Capital/EMI!
That's
highway
robbery,
and
you
know
it!
With
all
the
money
you've
already
made
on
the
Beatles'
catalog,
this
is
a
particular
heinous
crime.
</p>












<p>So,
Capital/EMI,
what
about
actually
remastering
the
Beatles
catalog?
They
are
only
considered
the
greatest
musical
force
of
the
last
half
of
the
20th
century.
The
Who's
catalog
has
been
remastered;
the
Byrds
catalog
has
been
remastered,
even
the
Hollies
catalog
was
wonderfully
remastered
for
their
box
set
(by
YOU
EMI!
).
It
seems
a
tragic,
bitter
irony
that
perhaps
the
most
musical
of
all
the
artists
of
the
60s
gets
the
shoddiest
of
digital
remastering.</p>












<p>As
far
as
the
actual
album
goes,
find
the
vinyl.
It
just
sounds
much
better,
better
bass,
much
less
harshness.
I've
got
the
Mobile
Fidelity
LP,
and
it
is
a
delight
to
listen
to.
I
probably
should
just
throw
away
my
CDs.
</p>












<p>As
for
the
raging
debate
between
Beatle
lovers
and
Beatle
haters
regarding
the
merits
of
this
album,
here
are
a
few
things
to
ponder:</p>












<p>This
album
was
made
as
the
Beatles
were
still
transitioning
from
having
a
manager
and
being
a
cohesive
unit
to
managing
themselves
(unwisely)
and
being
four
distinctly
different
people
with
less
and
less
in
common.
It
was
also
the
introduction
of
Yoko
to
the
ranks,
which
probably
really
hastened
the
split.
The
album
was
made
in
this
atmosphere
of
rapid
changing
dynamics
within
the
group.
It
was
also
made
over
quite
a
long
period
of
time:
May
through
October
of
'68.
The
fairly
close-knit
bunch
that
gathered
at
George's
home
to
make
demos
of
their
new
songs
in
May
were
disparate,
disenchanted
individuals
by
the
time
they
finished
the
album
in
October.
Much
has
been
made
of
them
recording
parts
of
this
album
separately.
That
only
became
true
towards
the
end
of
the
sessions,
and
only
because
they
had
gone
way
past
their
deadline
and
needed
to
finish
the
album
quickly.
Plus,
that
really
applied
mostly
to
overdubs.</p>












<p>So,
bottom
line
on
the
White
Album.
It
probably
does
go
on
too
long,
but
that
is
probably
part
of
its
charm.
There
is
certainly
no
other
album
in
the
Beatles
catalog
that
remotely
resembles
it.
Also
much
debate
over
the
inclusion
of
Revolution
9
-
does
it
belong
on
the
album?
Well,
it's
on
there,
and
I
suppose
that's
part
of
its
charm
as
well.
I
do
listen
to
it
from
time
to
time,
and
really,
it's
not
either
unlistenable
or
unmusical.
I
fact,
if
you've
had
the
unfortunate
experience
to
listen
to
any
of
John
&amp;
Yoko's
&quot;avant-garde&quot;
recordings,
you'll
find
this
MUCH
more
listenable.</p>












<p>In
the
end,
it's
down
to
the
songs,
and
how
they
are
performed
and
produced.
With
a
decent
remaster,
these
songs
stand
up,
performance
and
production-wise.
They
capture
the
songwriters
still
operating
at
peak
power
(much
time
and
inspiration
to
apply
to
their
craft
while
in
India).
In
fact,
John
said
more
than
once
that
he
was
very
proud
of
his
songs
on
the
White
Album.
I'm
sure
Macca
would
say
the
same.
Weaker
songs
like
Don't
Pass
Me
By
and
Long,
Long,
Long
add
to
the
character
and
mystique
of
the
album.
Goodnight
is
a
beautiful
lullaby,
the
perfect
antidote
to
Revolution
9
and
the
perfect
closer
for
the
album.
</p>












<p>The
white
album
is
an
oddessy.
It's
a
trip
through
many
musical
styles,
and
the
journey
of
a
group
whose
cracks
are
beginning
to
show;
albeit
in
a
charming
way.
I
certainly
don't
think
for
a
minute
this
is
their
best
work,
far
from
it.
But
the
stength
of
the
songs,
and
the
strength
of
the
band
itself,
show
through
and
make
this,
well,
another
essential
Beatles
album.</p>












<p>But
hold
out,
if
you
haven't
bought
it.
Force
Capital
/EMI
to
give
this
album
the
remaster
it
deserves.
</p>











</div>











</div>

<span

s_star_3_0
"
title="3.0
out
of

stars"><span>3.0
out
of
5
stars</span></span>












<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/review/RL4R1JWAPIZAN/ref=cm_cr_dp_title/187-8143282-8173756?ie=UTF8&amp;ASIN=B0025KVLU6&amp;nodeID=5174&amp;store=music"
class="txtlarge
gl3
gr4
reviewTitle
valignMiddle"><strong>A
five
star
album
given
a
one
star
treatment</strong></a>











<span
class="gry
valignMiddle">
<span
class="inlineblock
txtsmall">January
12,
2000</span>
</span>










</div>











<div
class="mt4
ath">











<span
class="gr10">
<span
class="txtsmall"><span
class="gry">By</span>
<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/pdp/profile/A37P63VA9MPXA5/ref=cm_cr_dp_pdp/187-8143282-8173756"
class="noTextDecoration">Brian
O'Marra</a></span>
</span>











</div>











<div
class="txtsmall
mt4
fvavp">











<span
class="inlineblock
formatVariation"><span
class="gr3
gry
formatKey">Format:</span><span
class="formatValue">Audio
CD</span></span>










</div>











<div
class="mt9
reviewText">












<div
class="drkgry">













The
above
rating
is
not
for
the
quality
of
the
Beatles'
performances.
The
album
rates
up
there
with
Sgt.
Pepper,
Revolver,
Rubber
Soul
and
Abbey
Road.












<p>Let
me
then
explain
why
it
deserves
the
rating.
At
the
time
of
its
initial
release
on
vinyl,
the
music
portrayed
an
encyclopedia
of
music
styles:
from
hard
rock
(Helter
Skelter),
to
blues
(Yer
Blues),
to
jazz
(Honey
Pie),
to
country
(Rocky
Raccoon),
to
Beach
Boys
surf
(Back
In
The
USSR).
</p>












<p>Its
cover
was
inspired
by
the
white
art
of
Yoko
and
individually
numbered
like
works
of
art.
In
fact
number
1
has
recently
turned
up.
Then
in
1987,
it
was
released
on
CD
on
two
separate
discs
packaged
together
in
a
longbox.</p>












<p>Then
later
it
was
repackaged
in
a
double
CD
clamshell
which
was
the
start
of
its
downfall.
It
listed
the
songs
for
Disc
One,
and
then
Dics
(sic)
Two.
As
far
as
I
am
aware
this
gaffe
still
exists.</p>












<p>Then
we
come
to
this
latest
repackaging.
Yes,
it
was
a
nice
way
to
commemorate
the
30th
anniversary
by
presenting
it
in
a
mini
album
format
complete
with
gatefold
sleeve,
poster,
and
four
mini
pictures
of
the
Beatles.
However,
one
begs
the
question:
why
wasn't
it
remastered?</p>












<p>Sgt.
Pepper
was
to
be
remastered
in
mono
for
its
30th
anniversary.
That
was
pulled
much
to
the
fans
displeasure.
Then
the
execs
at
Apple
didn't
want
to
pass
up
on
the
White
Album,
so
they
simple
dressed
up
the
packaging,
charged
extra,
and
left
the
remastering
circa
1987!</p>












<p>Why
not
put
out
the
mono
mix?
Piggies,
Blackbird,
Helter
Skelter,
Don't
Pass
Me
By
have
subtleties
that
would
sound
refreshing
today.</p>












<p>In
fact,
Happiness
is
A
Warm
Gun
in
mono
corrects
a
mixing
error
left
in
the
stereo.
The
instrumental
bridge
actually
had
John's
middle
8
sung
over
it.
He
actually
sang
that
twice.
However,
in
mixing
out
the
first
one
for
the
stereo
they
didn't
do
it
completely
because
you
can
hear
the
last
half
of
the
word
&quot;down&quot;
before
he
repeats
it.
The
mono
mixes
this
out
completely!</p>












<p>As
I
have
stated
before,
the
Beatles
catalog
demands
an
overhaul.
Maybe
if
enough
fans
complain,
we'll
see
it
happen!
</p>











</div>











</div>

vtStripe">

)
{








getElement("hmdFormDiv").style.display
=
"none";














getElement("hmdThanks").style.display
=
"";












}
else
if
(
result
==
"ERROR"
)
{








errorLayer.innerHTML
=
"There
was
an
error
processing
your
request.
Please
try
again
later.";






}
else
if
(
result
==
"COMMENT-LENGTH"
)
{








errorLayer.innerHTML
=
"Please
limit
your
comments
to
1000
characters.";






}




}







var
hmdResponseWarning
=
"Please
note
that
we
are
unable
to
respond
directly
to
all
feedback
submitted
via
this
form,
but
we'll
ask
you

sign
in
so
we
can
contact
you
if
needed.

Feedback
is
limited
to
1000
characters.";





function
hmdProcessSubmit(hmdForm)
{






if(hmdForm.comment.value
==
""
||










hmdForm.comment.value
==
hmdResponseWarning)
{
	

alert
("Please
enter
some
feedback
before
clicking
Submit.");
	

return
false;	






}







hmdForm.type.value
=
'pipeline';
//





hmdForm.target
=
'iFrameHMD';	
//





hmdForm.type.value
=
'if';













hmdForm.jsEnabled.value
=
'1';






hmdPopulateArgs();








return
true;




}





function
limitTextLength(field,
limit){








if(field.value.length
>
limit){












field.value
=
field.value.substring(0,
limit);












field.scrollTop
=
field.scrollHeight;








}




}





function
clearHmdInitialText(field){








if(field.value==hmdResponseWarning){












field.value="";








}




}
//--></script>

=

=

var

=
function
()
{








if
(

window.RECS_rhfShvlLoaded












&&
!

&&
$('#rhf_container').size()
>

+

=

{
















rhfPosition
-=
$(window).scrollTop();












}

(rhfElementFound
&&
(
rhfPosition
-

))
{
















window.RECS_rhfMetrics["start"]
=
(new

window.RECS_rhfShvlLoading
=

=

=

};
















var

()
{

=

};

amznJQ.onReady('jQuery',
function()
{


var
voteAjaxDefaultBeforeSendReviews
=
function(buttonAnchor,
buttonContainer,
messageContainer)
{




messageContainer.html('Sending
feedback...');





buttonContainer.hide();





messageContainer.show();


};


var
voteAjaxDefaultSuccessReviews
=
function(aData,
aStatus,
buttonAnchor,
buttonContainer,
messageContainer,
isNoButton)
{





if
(aData.redirect
==
1)
{






return
window.location.href=buttonAnchor.children[0].href;




}




if
(aData.error
==
1)
{






jQuery(buttonContainer.children()[0]).html('Sorry,
we
failed
to
record
your
vote.
Please
try
again');






messageContainer.hide();






buttonContainer.show();




}
else
{






messageContainer.html('Thank
you
for
your
feedback.');






if
(isNoButton
==
1)
{








messageContainer.append('<span
class="black
gl5">If
this
review
is
inappropriate,
<a
href="http://www.amazon.com/gp/voting/cast/Reviews/2115/R170AARLNZ9D3M/Inappropriate/1/ref=cm_cr_dp_abuse_voteyn/187-8143282-8173756?ie=UTF8&target=&token=C696849F61F3614887D5C45DF0DFC795A8C61B5A&voteAnchorName=R170AARLNZ9D3M.2115.Inappropriate.Reviews&voteSessionID=187-8143282-8173756"
class="noTextDecoration"
style="color:
#039;"
>please
let
us
know.</a></span>');






}






messageContainer.addClass('green');




}


};


var
voteAjaxDefaultErrorReviews
=
function(aStatus,
aError,
buttonAnchor,
buttonContainer,
messageContainer)
{





jQuery(buttonContainer.children()[0]).html('Sorry,
we
failed
to
record
your
vote.
Please
try
again');




messageContainer.hide();




buttonContainer.show();


};



jQuery('.votingButtonReviews').each(function(){




jQuery(this).unbind('click.vote.Reviews');




jQuery(this).bind('click.vote.Reviews',
function(){






var
buttonAnchor
=
this;






var
buttonContainer
=
jQuery(this).parent();






var
messageContainer
=
jQuery(buttonContainer).next('.votingMessage');






var
isNoButton
=
jQuery(this).hasClass('noButton');






jQuery.ajax({








type:
'GET',








dataType:
'json',








ajaxTimeout:
10000,








cache:
false,








beforeSend:
function(){











voteAjaxDefaultBeforeSendReviews(buttonAnchor,
buttonContainer,
messageContainer);









},








success:
function(data,
textStatus){











voteAjaxDefaultSuccessReviews(data,
textStatus,
buttonAnchor,
buttonContainer,
messageContainer,
isNoButton);









},








error:
function(XMLHttpRequest,
textStatus,
errorThrown){










voteAjaxDefaultErrorReviews(textStatus,
errorThrown,
buttonAnchor,
buttonContainer,
messageContainer);








},








url:
buttonAnchor.children[0].href+'&type=json'






});






return
false;




});


});
});
